TIDY

Keeping fields that are needed for my analysis and removing others as first step and using mutate change OCCUR_DATE datatype from character to Date.

I am using below fields for my analysis. - INCIDENT_KEY - PERP_SEX - VIC_SEX - PERP_AGE_GROUP - VIC_AGE_GROUP - BORO - OCCUR_TIME - OCCUR_DATE - STATISTICAL_MURDER_FLAG

nypd_input <- nypd_input %>%
select(-c(LOCATION_DESC,PRECINCT,PERP_RACE,JURISDICTION_CODE,VIC_RACE,
          X_COORD_CD,Y_COORD_CD,Latitude,Longitude)) %>%=20
mutate(OCCUR_DATE =3D mdy(OCCUR_DATE))

ANALYSIS

Total incidents Borough wise and year

Incidents_by_boro_year <- nypd_inp=
ut %>%=20
  mutate(year =3D lubridate::year(OCCUR_DATE)) %>%
    group_by(BORO, year) %>%
    summarize(total_incidents_by_year =3D n()) %>%
ungroup()

u can override using the

slicing

#Now, calculate Total Incidents by Borough and the year having maximum incidents

Incidents_by_boro <- nypd_input %&=
gt;%
group_by(BORO,year =3D lubridate::year(OCCUR_DATE))  %>%
summarize(total_incidents =3D n()) %>%
mutate(max_year =3D year[which.max(total_incidents)]) %>%
summarize(total_incidents =3D sum(total_incidents),
year_with_max_incidents =3D first(max_year)) %>%
select(BORO, total_incidents, year_with_max_incidents) %>%
ungroup()
## `summarise()` has grouped output by 'BORO'. Yo=
u can override using the
## `.groups` argument.
Incidents_by_boro
## # A tibble: 5 =C3=97 3
##   BORO          total_incidents year_with_max_incidents
##   <chr>                   <int>                   <dbl>=
;
## 1 BRONX                    7937                    2021
## 2 BROOKLYN                10933                    2006
## 3 MANHATTAN                3572                    2021
## 4 QUEENS                   4094                    2008
## 5 STATEN ISLAND             776                    2008

joining

Now, I am joining this dataframe =E2=80=98Incidents_by_boro=E2=80=99 wit= h =E2=80=98Incidents_by_boro_year=E2=80=99 to get result borough wise total i= ncidents along with year that has maximum incidents and incident count in that year borough wise

final_incidents_rep_boro <- Incide=
nts_by_boro %>%=20
  left_join(Incidents_by_boro_year ,by =3D c("B=
ORO", "year_with_max_incidents"=

Incidents_by_boro_ranked <- Incide= nts_by_boro %>% arrange(desc(total_incidents)) %>% mutate(BORO =3D factor(BORO, levels =3D BORO)) %>% mutate(boro_ranking =3D row_number()) # Create a color palette colors <- c("red", "orange", "lightcoral",= "yellow", "= green") # Plotting ggplot(Incidents_by_boro_ranked, aes(x =3D BORO, y =3D total_incidents, fil= l =3D BORO)) + geom_bar(stat =3D "identity") + scale_fill_manual(values =3D colors) + geom_text(aes(label =3D total_incidents), vjust =3D -0.5) + geom_hline(yintercept =3D max(Incidents_by_boro_ranked$total_incidents), = linetype =3D "dashed", color =3D "red") + ggtitle("Total Incidents by Borough") = + xlab("Borough") + ylab("Total Incidents")

LINEAR MODEL based on gender to year

A Linear Mode which predicts the no.of incidents by victim gender=3D=E2= =80=98M=E2=80=99 by year. This model uses the existing data to predict the outcome, which has been compared with the real outcomes.

incident_count_vic_sex <- nypd_inp=
ut %>% filter(STATISTICAL_MURDER_FLAG =3D=3D 'TRUE') %>%
  group_by(BORO,year =3D lubridate::year(OCCUR_DATE)) %>%
  summarise(total_incidents =3D n(),
            total_incidents_M =3D sum(VIC_SEX =3D=3D 'M', na.rm =3D TRUE),
            total_incidents_F =3D sum(VIC_SEX =3D=3D 'F', na.rm =3D TRUE)) %>=
;%
select(BORO, year, total_incidents_M, total_incidents_F) %>%
ungroup()
## `summarise()` has grouped output by 'BORO'. Yo=
u can override using the
## `.groups` argument.
incident_count_vic_sex
## # A tibble: 85 =C3=97 4
##    BORO   year total_incidents_M total_incidents_F

t;

##  2 BRONX  2007                85                 8

using the data above, below is the prediction for Borough BRONX

#predict=
ion
mod_data <- incident_count_vic_sex %>% filter(BORO =3D=3D "BRONX")
mod <- lm(year ~ total_incidents_M,data =3D mod_data)
pred_data <- mod_data %>% mutate(pred =3D predict(mod))
pred_data %>% ggplot() +
 ggtitle("MANHATTAN") +=20
 geom_point(aes(x =3D year,y =3D total_incidents_M),color =3D "blue") + =20
 geom_point(aes(x =3D year,y =3D pred),color =3D "red")

BIAS

Inaccuracies or missing data can introduce bias. certain incidents may be excluded based on certain criteria. With increasing data volume, differences in reporting rates over the years can lead to biased trends. Sometimes changes in law or policies might lead to variations in how incidents are recorded over time.

Project Conclusion

By analyzing the pie charts, graphs, and models I generated above, I am able to find the rise or fall in the number of incidents based on boroughs and then by states by year. I identified the borough with the highest number of incidents overall and also visualized the ratio of each gender in both victims and perpetrators compared to the other.
